784	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Bangladesh and others Vs. Md. Nazrul Islam &amp; others, (Md. Nuruzzaman, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NO. 3584 OF 2018   </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Hasan Foez Siddique, J, Zinat Ara, J, Md. Nuruzzaman, J, </p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Samarendra Nath Biswas, Deputy Attorney General, instructed by Mr. Haridas Paul, Advocate-on-Record ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ AD</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Government of Bangladesh and others  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Nazrul Islam and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Constitution of Bangladesh </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 118px;" width="566"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 249.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Zinat Ara, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Government of Bangladesh and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">. . . <u>Petitioners</u></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Md. Nazrul Islam and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . .<u>Respondents</u></span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12pt 0.85pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: left;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: left;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Teachers and staffs of the Non-Government School and College could not claim the M.P.O. as a matter of right and as such, </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">direction could not be given unless infringement</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> of legal right or violation of law.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>. . . (14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Abdur Rahman Vs. Bangladesh 10 BLC (AD) 179;</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Government Vs. K. M. Ekbal Hossen and others in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 3882 of 2018;</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Secretary, Ministry of Education and others Vs. Md. Saidur Rahman in Civil Petition for Leave Appeal No. 2584 of 2018 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">For the Petitioners </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">: Mr. Samarendra Nath Biswas, Deputy Attorney <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">General, instructed by Mr. Haridas </span>Paul, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">For the Respondents : </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">Not presented</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in .85pt 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-variant: small-caps;">Md. Nuruzzaman, <span style="color: black;">j</span></span></u></strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">:</span></u> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">Delay of 230 (Two hundred thirty) days in filing of the Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 17675 of 2017 is hereby condoned.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">This Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal has been preferred against the judgment and order dated 25.01.2018 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.17675 of 2017 disposing the Rule Nisi and thereby directing the writ respondents to release the Government portion of salary (M.P.O.) of the writ petitioners with arrear and other service benefit from the date of joining, if any, within 1(one) month on receipt of the judgment and order without any fail.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">The facts leading to filing of this Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal, in short, are that, the present respondents herein as writ petitioners filed Writ Petition No.17675 of 2017 before the High Court Division seeking direction upon the writ respondents/ authorities to release the Monthly Payment Order (in short M.P.O.) of the writ petitioners with arrear and other service benefit from the date of joining stating that after completion of all the requirements, the writ petitioner No.1-Md. Nazrul Islam was appointed as Lecturer of Bengali on 08.10.2006 and he joined his post on 10.10.2006; the writ petitioner No.2-Naima Fedausy was appointed as Lecturer of English on 31.01.2008 and she joined her post on 31.01.2008; the writ petitioner No.3-Abu Jafur Md. Rafikullah was appointed as Lecturer of Islamic Studies on 08.10.2006 and he joined his post on 10.10.2006; the writ petitioner No.4-Md. Salim Khan was appointed as lecturer of Islamic History &amp; Culture on 08.10.2006 and he joined his post on 10.10.2006; the writ petitioner No.5-Mahafuja Sultana was appointed as Lecturer of Social Welfare/works on 30.12.2014 and she joined her post on 01.01.2015; the writ petitioner No.6-Md. Monzur Alam was appointed as Lecturer of Political Science on 10.08.2015 and he joined his post on 11.08.2015; the writ petitioner No.7-Mohammad Kamal Hossain appointed as Lecturer of Economics on 10.08.2015 and he joined his post on 11.08.2015; the writ petitioner No.8-Nadira Sultana was appointed as lecturer of Philosophy on 10.08.2015 and she joined her post on 11.08.2015; the writ petitioner No.9-Md. Abdus Salam Bepari was appointed as 4<sup>th</sup> Class employee on 08.10.2006 and he joined his post on 10.10.2006; the writ petitioner No.10-Md. Alamgir was appointed as 4<sup>th</sup> Class employee on 08.10.2006 and he joined his post on 10.10.2006 and the writ petitioner No.11-Md. Chunnu Rari was appointed as 4<sup>th</sup> class employee on 08.10.2006 and he joined his post on 10.10.2006. Since their joining in the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Engineer Faruk Talukder Mohila Degree College, Bhouphal, Patuakhali they have been working and discharging their duties full satisfaction of the authority concerned in the said college till today; that the Principal of the concerned college sent a proposal to the writ respondent No.2, that is, the Director General, Directorate of Secondary and Higher Secondary Education, Dhaka requesting him to grant their Government portion of salary with necessary papers but the enlistment of the writ petitioners’ name in the Monthly Pay Order (M.P.O.) has not yet been approved by the concerned authority. But the writ respondent No.2 has already allowed the Monthly Pay Order (M.P.O.) of other lecturers and staffs of the said college. Under the aforesaid facts and circumstances, the writ petitioners served a legal notice upon the writ respondents seeking redress but in vain. Hence, the writ petitioners, finding no other alternative efficacious remedy, filed the instant writ petition before the </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">High Court Division </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">and obtained the Rule Nisi.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">The writ respondents did not contest the Rule Nisi by filing any affidavit-in-opposition.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">             </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">In due course, after hearing the writ petitioners and considering the connected papers on record, a Division Bench of the High Court Division disposed of the Rule Nisi by the impugned judgment and order dated </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">25.01.2018. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">Feeling aggrieved, by the judgment and order dated 25.01.2018 passed in Writ Petition No.17675 of 2017 the Government and others-writ respondents as petitioners herein filed the instant civil Petition for leave to appeal.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">Mr. Samarendra Nath Biswas, the learned Deputy Attorney General appearing on behalf of the leave-petitioners submits that the High Court Division failed to apply its judicial mind in passing the impugned judgment and order and thereby exceeded its jurisdiction in directing to includes the name of the writ petitioners in the Monthly Payment Order because the appointment of the writ petitioners have been done without any approval from the concerned authority as well as the writ petitioners are teachers and staffs beyond the pattern of M.P.O. of the said College. The Engineer Faruk Talukder Mohila Degree College, Bhouphal, Patuakhali have only M.P.O. enlistment upto the higher secondary level, that is, the Intermediate level and not upto degree level. According to provision of law of Jonobal Kathamo of the Higher Secondary level college, there would be only one teacher in each subject. The College has already filled up the M.P.O. for one teacher in each subject in the Intermediate level. Hence, there is no scope to enlist them in the M.P.O. list as teachers of degree level which are beyond the pattern of college, and as such, the impugned judgment and order passed by the High Court Division is liable to be set aside. He further submits that the financial sanction of Government is dependent upon the policy mater of the Government for which no writ petition is maintainable in the present form challenging the policy of the Government and, as such, the impugned judgment and order passed by the High Court Division is liable to be set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">We have considered the submissions of the learned Deputy Attorney General for the leave petitioners. Perused the impugned judgment and order of the High Court Division and connected papers on record.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">The case of the writ petitioners is that they are entitled to have M.P.O. as they have already completed all the formalities and criteria to have the same. They further claimed that although other teachers have the M.P.O. of the same College but their case is not considered by the concerned authority. They served the legal notice but in vain. Hence, they filed the writ petition for redress. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.</span></span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;"><span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;">The question is whether the writ petitioners have any legal right to have the M.P.O. as teachers of the said College and they are legally entitled to invoke the</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%;"> jurisdiction of writ of Mandamus for direction upon the writ respondents to include their names in the M.P.O. list of the College.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">In Abdur Rahman Vs. Bangladesh 10 BLC (AD) 179 held that “Mandamus may issue where there is a violation of a legal right or violation of a legal duty. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">Earlier, this Division, in the case of Government Vs. K. M. Ekbal Hossen and others in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.3882 of 2018, has observed: </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">“The legislature, executive and judiciary have to functions with their own spheres demarcated under the Constitution. No organ can usurp the functions assigned to another. Function of democracy depends upon the strength of independency of State organs. Legislature and executive <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">have the powers maintenance, distribution </span>and control of finance of the State. Judiciary has the power to examine and to ensure that aforesaid two organs of the State functionaries have been working within their constitutional limits and in accordance with law. The constitution does not permit the Court to direct or advice the executive in the matter of policy or to sermonize qua any matter which under the constitution lies within the sphere of legislature or executive, provided these authorities do not transgress their constitutional limits or statutory powers. Judiciary also must <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">guard against encroaching the limitations</span>. The scope of Judicial enquiry is confined to the question whether the decision taken by the Government is against any statutory provisions or is violative of the fundamental rights of the citizens or is opposed to the provisions of the Constitution. It is the executive and legislature who are entitled to frame policies and take such administrative decision as they think necessary in the public interest. The Court should not ordinarily interfere with policy decisions, unless clearly illegal or unconstitutional”.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">This Division same view has expressed in the case of Government represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Education and others Vs. Md. Saidur Rahman in Civil Petition for Leave Appeal No.2584 of 2018 and further has held that-</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-left: 27.35pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 115%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">“Here, in this case, the High Court Division </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">in fact, passed the impugned order to compel</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">the executive to pay Government portion of salaries inasmuch as the Government did decide as yet to pay salaries to them or even did not assure them that the Government would pay the same. In absence of the statutory obligation, the High Court Division under Article 102 of the Constitution is not justified in issuing mandamus for payment of salary since a mandamus cannot lie in the absence of a legal right based on the existence of statutory duty. The mere fact that recognition and registration have been granted to an institutions or, for that matter, for conducting new course or <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">subject would not give rise to a presumption</span><span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> of a financial sanction. A financial liability</span> cannot be foisted on the Government to </span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">reimburse the salary payable to the teachers and staffs of the private colleges on the basis of such presumption. No mandamus can issue for payment of salary by the Government in the absence of the prior sanction of the Government”.</span><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“According to “Dicey”, Judges are not allowed to decide a case on the basis of whatever they consider just and fair. <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">They are constrained by definite principles</span> of law and by binding precedent”.     </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">14.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case in hand the petitioners did not allege that the writ respondents have violated any legal right of them. The granting of M.P.O. is the policy decision of the Government. Therefore, the petitioners could not claim the same as of right. This Division is of the view that teachers and staffs of the Non-Government School and College could not claim the M.P.O. as a matter of right and as such, direction could not be given unless infringement of legal right or violation of law. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">15.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the foregoing discussions and authorities, we are of the considered view that the instant writ petition is not maintainable. We find merit in the petition, however, we are not inclined to grant leave, rather, dispose of the instant Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal as the writ petition was not maintainable.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">16.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Accordingly, this petition is disposed of. The judgment and order of the High Court Division is set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in .85pt 12.0pt 0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__August__2019(2)/Issue__August_19__C.%20P.%203584%20of%2018__Md.%20Nuruzzaman_J___AD___2_.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; font-variant: small-caps; color: black;">Civil Petition For Leave To Appeal No.</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; font-variant: small-caps; color: black;"> 3584 of 2018 </span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">(From the judgment and order dated 25.01.2018 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.17675 of 2017)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
785	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Bangladesh Vs. Md. Ali Ashraf Khondoker &amp; ors., (Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 3849 of 2010  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Ensan Uddin Sheikh, A.A.G. with Ms. Afifa Begum, A.A.G.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Government of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh Represented by the Deputy Commissioner Sirajgonj </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Ali Ashraf Khondoker and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  State Acquisition and Tenancy Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; font-variant: small-caps;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></span></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 228px;" width="535"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 235.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.3pt; font-style: normal;">Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> </span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Judgment on</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">07.03.2018</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 42.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__August__2019(2)/Issue%20__August__19(2)__C.%20Rule%203849%20of%2010_Md.%20Moinul%20Islam%20Chowdhury,%20J.__4.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 213.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Government of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh Represented by the Deputy Commissioner Sirajgonj</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . Defendant-Respondent -Petitioner </span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">=Versus=</span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Md. Ali Ashraf Khondoker and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . Plaintiffs-Appellant-Opposite Parties </span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">State Acquisition and Tenancy Act (XXVIII of 1950)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 86</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 86 Sub-Section 2 before amendment was that suit land would be considered as alleviated and remained under water for more than 20 years prior to the amendment of Act 1950 Sub-Section 4. However, after amendment of the said Section 86 in the year of 1994 the time period has been fixed that an owner of the land could only loose the right by diluvion if such land reappeared within 30 years. In the instant case the present Government petitioner claimed that the suit land was alleviated around the year of 1982 from river Fuljor, as such, the provision before amendment in the year of 1994 would be applicable which was earlier 20 years for the period of diluvion and aluvion. Therefore as the land was diluviated in the year of 1956 and alleviated in the year of 1982 the land remained under water for more than 26 years which is beyond 20 years period of time, as such, the record of right in S.A. and R.S. in the name of Government as khas Khatinan No. 1 has been done as per the operation of law and the present plaintiff opposite parties lost their right and title by the said provisions of law. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>. . .(18)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">Mr. Md. Ensan Uddin Sheikh, A.A.G. with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Ms. Afifa Begum, A.A.G.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . .For the Petitioner </span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Md. Asaduzzaman with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Md. Anisul Hassan with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Ms. Farhana Islam Khan with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Md. Salequzzaman and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Abdullah-Al- Mahmud, Advocates</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .For the Opposite Party Nos. 1-5 </span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11pt;">At <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the instance of the present defendant-respondent</span> <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">petitioner, Government of the People’s Republic</span> of Bangladesh Represented by the Deputy Commissioner, Sirajgonj, this Rule has been issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the judgment and decree dated 05.04.2007complained of in the petition moved in court should not be set aside. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">The Rule is directed against the judgment</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;"> and decree dated 05.04.2007 passed by learned Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Sirajgonj in Other Class Appeal No. 53 of 2004 allowed the appeal reversing the judgment and decree dated 29.02.2004 passed by the learned <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Assistant Judge, Raygonj Assistant Judge Court</span>, Sirajgonj in Other Class Suit No. 90 of 2002.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The relevant facts for disposal of this Rule, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter-alia,</em> are that the present opposite parties as the plaintiffs filed the Other Class Suit No. 90 of 2002 in the court of learned Assistant Judge, Raygonj, Sirajgonj for declaration of title upon the land describe in the schedule of the plaint. The case in the plaint is that the suit land appertaining to C.S.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Khatian No. 99 as describe in the plaint as schedule ‘Ka’ and the land in D.S. Khatain No. 101 describe in the plaint as schedule ‘Kha’ was originally owned by the predecessors of the plaintiffs. The C.S. record of right was published and the plaintiffs have been in possession upon the land measuring 3.49 acres in D.S. Plot Nos. 1003, 1458 and 968. Under C.S. Khatian No. 101 but during S.A. operation some portion of plaintiffs land was not recorded properly and during R.S. operation the property was recorded in the name of the present defendant petitioner, the Government of Bagnaldesh, as such, as the plaintiffs filed the suit claiming entitlement upon the entire land.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The present petitioner as the defendant No. 1 and another defendant No. 2 contested the suit by filing a written statement contending, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter-alia</em>, that after the C.S. record of right the suit land described in the plaint as schedule ‘Gha’ became diluviated which was subsequently alluviated, as such, under the operation of law the suit property was vested <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">upon the Government, accordingly, the land was</span> properly and correctly recorded in the name of Government during R.S. operation. The present opposite party filed the suit by creating some <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">false documents in order to grab the Government</span> land which has been under possession through allotment to the landless people.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">After hearing the parties and considering the documentary evidence as well as the deposition of the witnesses on behalf of the respective parties dismissed the suit by the judgment and decree dated 29.02.2004. Being aggrieved the present opposite parties as the appellants preferred the Other Class Appeal No. 53 of 2004 in the court of learned District Judge, Sirajgonj which was heard by the learned Joint District Judge, court No. 1, Sirajgonj who by his judgment and decree dated 05.04.2007 allowed the appeal by reversing and setting aside the judgment and decree of the trial court. This revisional application has been filed under Section 115 (1) of the Code of Civil Procedure challenging the legality of the said impugned judgment passed by the appellate court below and the present Rule was issued thereupon.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">Mr. Md. Ensan Uddin Sheikh, the learned</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> Assistant Attorney General, appearing with the learned Assistant Attorney General, Ms. Afifa Begum, submits that the learned lower appellate court committed an error of law occasioning failure of justice in not considering that the S.A. and R.S. record of the suit land was correctly prepared in the name of the Government within the knowledge of all concern and the plaintiffs never came before the court of settlement for correcting those record and as such the impugned judgment is liable to be s et aside.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Assistant Attorney General further submits that the learned trial court came to a lawful conclusion to dismiss the suit filed by the present opposite parties upon the given facts that the suit land was diluviated and became river Fuljor around the year of 1956. The<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>river was thereafter alluvited around the year of 1982(after 20 years) therefore, pursuant to Sections 86 and 87 of the State Acquisition and Tenancy Act, 1950 and also pursuant to the President Order No. 135 of 1972 the suit property was vested upon the present Government-petitioner. Accordingly, land was recorded in the R.S. Khatian No. 1 in the name of Government as the Khash land. As such, the learned court came to a lawful conclusion to dismissed the suit whereas the learned appellate court without considering the document produced by the present petitioner- Government regarding diluvion and alluvion of the suit land came to a wrongful conclusion because the plaintiffs failed to prove their own case, as such, this court should interfere upon the impugned judgment and the Rule should be made absolute. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The Rule has been opposed by the present opposite parties.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Asaduzzaman, the learned Advocate, appearing with the learned Advocates Mr. Md. Anisul Hassan, Ms. Farhana Islam Khan, Mr. Md. Salequzzaman and Mr. Abdullah-Al- Mahmud, for the opposite parties, submits that the learned<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>trial court considered that the present opposite parties lawfully succeeded the land and there was no bar to filed the suit under the limitation period but wrongfully found that the plaintiff did not take appropriate steps for proving continuation of title and the record of right in C.S. Dag Nos. 99 and 101 upon the land measuring 2.80 acres along with the other land which were not diluviated under river Fuljor in District Sirajgonj. However, the learned appellate court below properly found that there was no diluviation of the suit land as other neighboring plots were in the name of other private persons. Therefore, including the scheduled property under S.A. and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>R.S. Khatian No. 1 as the Government Property was absolutely wrong on the part of the Government, as such, the record of right published in the name of Government of the suit land was absolutely misconceived and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>incorrect and the learned appellate court passed the impugned judgment and decree on the basis of law and this court should not interfere upon the impugned judgment and decree and the Rule should be discharged.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate further submits that the present opposite parties produced Exhibits-3 and 3(Ka) in the appellate court under Order 41 Rule 27 of the Code of Civil Procedure, therefore, the learned trial court did not have any chance to examine those vital documents, thus, the record of right in S.A. and R.S. in favour of the Government under Section 86 of the State Acquisition and Tenancy Act. A property can only be vested after 30(thirty) years from the date of diluviation but the present petitioner-Government claimed that suit land was alluviated in the year of 1982 which is less than 30 years, as such, the learned trial court committed an error of law regarding diluviation, whereas, the learned appellate court came to a correct decision.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Considering the above submissions made by the learned Advocates appearing for the respective parties and also considering the revisional application filed under Section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure along with the annexures therein, in particular, the impugned judgment and decree passed by the learned appellate court and also after perusal of the materials in<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>the lower court records, it appears to me that the present opposite parties as the plaintiffs filed the title suit for declaration of title upon the suit land described in the schedule of the plaint. The plaintiffs case was that one Hanif Uddin Khondoker was<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span>the C.S. recorded owner of land measuring 10.46 acres who died leaving behind his son Harun Uddin Khondoker who also died leaving behind 5 sons being Rawsan Ali and others. By way of succession and purchase the plaintiffs became owners but in the S.A. and R.S. record the land was recorded in the name of the present petitioner-Government, as such, the suit was filed challenging the publication of record of right which was clouded their entitlement. On the other hand, the present petitioner as the defendant contended that in the C.S. record the suit land was in the private names but during the operation of S.A. record the suit land was diluviated and turned into the river Fuljor and the land remained under water for a long period of time. However, S.A. record of right was published in the name of the than Purba Pakistan province represented by Collector of Pabna (exhibit-Ka) accordingly R.S. record of right was published in the name of Government sometime after 1982 when the suit land was alluviated and R.S. record of right in the name of the present petitioner-Government (exhibit-“Ka-1”), therefore, the present plaintiffs opposite parties do not have any right and title upon the suit land. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above conflicting factual aspects between the parties, this court has to take a legal decision in the case as to the entitlement of the suit land described in the plaint. In this regard I have carefully examined and considered the documents adduced and produced by the parties in support of their respective cases. There is no dispute that C.S. recorded tenant Hanif Uddin Khondoker and his son Harun Uddin Khondaker was C.S. recorded tenant but the land became subject matter of diluviation around the year of 1956 and the land turned into the river Fuljor and the land remain undered water. However the present plaintiff-opposite parties claimed that the land of C.S. Khatian Nos. 99 and 101 being Dag No. 1458, 1003 and 968 total land measuring 3.49 acres were not subject matter of diluviated and they remained in possession. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">However, I found difficulty as to possession of the present opposite parties upon the suit land as there is no payment of Khajna or any other documents for proving the possession upon the suit land by the present plaintiff opposite parties. In this regard the government petitioner claimed that the land was under water since 1956, as such, no question arises for possession by the present plaintiff opposite parties. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">However, the Government could prove that the land was under water, as S.A. record was published in the name of petitioner-Government. In addition to S.A. record of right, R.S. record of right was also consistently published in the name of the Government petitioner which is the relevant document to show that the land was diluviated and it was alluviated after the year of 1992 when Section 86 (3) of the State Acquisition and Tenancy Act and President Order No. 135 of 1972 remained as the operative<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and prevailing law.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Under Section 86 of the Act, 1950, the Government acquired right by operation of law of any land which is subject to diluvion and allevion. Accordingly, Section 86 sub- Section 1 and 2 of the Act, 1950 are relevant in the present case which reads as follows:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“1[86. Abatement of rent on account of <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>diluvion and determination of right in land re-appeared on account of alluvion-(1) If the lands of a holding or a portion of such lands are lost by diluvion, the rent or the land development tax of holding shall, on application or intimation made by the tenant in the prescribed from to the Revenue officer, be abated by such amount as may be considered by the Revenue officer<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>to be fair and equitable in accordance with the rules made in this behalf by the Government and the act of such loss by diluvion shall be recorded in accordance with such rules, which shall be treated as proof of title to the lands when the same re-appear in situ.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(2) Notwithstanding anything contained in any other law for the time being in force, the right, title and interest of the original tenant or his successor-in-interest shall subsist in the lands or a holding or portion thereof during the period of loss by diluvion if such lands re-appear in situ within thirty years of their loss. ”<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span></span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In addition to the above law after liberation of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Bangladesh<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Order No. 3 of the President Order No. 135 of 1972 also provided provisions for alluvion and diluvion which reads as follows: </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“(3)All lands, so lost by diluvion under sub-section (2), which re-appeared before the date of commencement of the said Order, but in respect of which the right of the tenant,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>whose land was so lost or his successors-in-interest, to re-possession was not finally recognized or declared by a competent authority or Court under any law for the time being in force and also all lands, so lost by diluvion under the said sub-section, which may be re-appear on or after the said date, shall vest absolutely in the Government free from all encumbrances and shall be at its disposal.”</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above two provisions of law, I have examined the present case and found that the plaintiff opposite parties could not<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>prove absolute possession upon the suit land by way of inheritance because the suit land was subject matter of diluvion and alluvion the plaintiffs do not have any entitlement upon suit land. In this regard, the Government-petitioner produced Exhibit-Ka and Exhibit-(Ka)1 as to the record of right in S.A. and R.S. therefore it can be taken that the land was subject to diluvion and alluvion.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Now, the question is whether the plaintiffs have lost their entitlement only because of diluvion and alluvion. In this regard Section 86 Sub-Section 2 before amendment was that suit land would be considered as alluviated and remained under water for more than 20 years prior to the amendment of Act 1950 Sub-Section 4. However, after amendment of the said Section 86 in the year of 1994 the time period has been fixed that an owner of the land could only loose the right by diluvion if such land reappeared within 30 years. In the instant case the present Government petitioner claimed that the suit land was alluviated around the year of 1982 from river Fuljor, as such, the provision before amendment in the year of 1994 would be applicable which was earlier 20 years for the period of diluvion and alluvion. Therefore<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>as the land was diluviated in the year of 1956 and alluviated in the year of 1982 the land remained under water for more than 26 years which is beyond 20 years period of time, as such, the record of right in S.A. and R .S. in the name of Government as khash Khatian No. 1 has been done as per the operation of law and the present plaintiff opposite parties lost their right<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and title by the said provisions of law.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">I am now inclined to examine the judgment and decree passed by the learned courts below. The learned trial court came to a conclusion to dismiss the suit filed by the present plaintiff opposite parties on the basis of the following findings:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: BurigangaSushreeMJ;">“h¡c£fr e¡¢m¢n S¢j cMm L­l j­jÑ h¡c£ f­rl pLm p¡r£Ne c¡¢h L­l ¢f, X¢hÔE-1 ®Sl¡u Sh¡­h h­me p¡­hL 1458 c¡­N 280 HLl 1003 c¡­N 31 naL J 968 c¡­N 38 naL S¢jz</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: BurigangaSushreeMJ;">A¡l¢S­a E­õ¢Ma ‘L’ J ‘M’ af¢pm fkÑ¡­m¡Qe¡u ®cM¡ k¡u ®k af¢p­m ¢p, Hp, 99 J 100 ew M¢au¡­el ®L¡b¡uJ 1458c¡N Hhw f¢lj¡e 2|80 HLl Hl X~­õM e¡C<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>p¤al¡w ‘M’ af¢pm h¢ZÑa 1458 c¡­Nl 2|80 HLl S¢j L af¢p­ml A¿¹NÑa j­jÑ c¡¢h fËj¡¢ea qu e¡C g­m h¡c£fr e¡¢m¢n S¢j cMm L­l j­jÑ p¡r£ N­el p¡rÉ<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>à¡l¡ h¡c£fr ­L¡e i¡­hC m¡ih¡e qJu¡l pñhe¡ e¡Cm h¡c£ f­rl c¡¢hL«a‘M’ af¢p­ml p¡L¥mÉ S¢j e¡¢m¢n ¢p, Hp 99<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>J 101 ew M¢au¡­el A¿¹NÑa e­q AbÑv 1458 c¡­Nl 2|80 HLl S¢jl f§hÑhaÑ£ j¡¢mL h¡c£N­el f§hÑhaÑ£ q¡¢eg E¢Ÿe J q¡l¦e E¢Ÿe M¾cL¡­ll ¢Rm h¡c£ fr a¡q¡ fËj¡e L¢l­a prj qe e¡Cz”</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On the other hand the learned appellate courts below allowed the appeal wrongfully thereby set aside the judgment and decree passed by learned trial court on the basis of the following unlawful findings:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: BurigangaSushreeMJ;">“ e¡¢mn£ S¢jl Q¡l f¡­nÅl S¢j pj§q Bl, Hp,®lL­XÑ fËS¡­cl e¡­j ®lLXÑ qJu¡u Eš² e¡¢m¢n S¢j plL¡­ll e¡­j M¡p M¢au¡­e ®lLXÑ qJu¡u ®L¡e ¢i¢š M¤­S f¡Ju¡ k¡u e¡z<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Q¡¢lf¡­n fËS¡­cl e¡¢ju ®lLXÑ ïj¡aÈL j­jÑ plL¡l ¢hh¡c£ a¡q¡­cl p¡­rÉ c¡¢h L­l e¡z<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>h¡c£fr Bl¢S­a e¡¢m¢n ¢p,Hp, 968 c¡­Nl S¢j Bl, Hp La ejÅl c¡­N ®lLXÑ q­u­R a¢ào­u ¢LR¤ E­õM L­l e¡Cz Hacü­aÄJ ¢X,X¡¢hÔE-1 ®Sl¡u S¡e¡u ®k Eš² S¢j Bl, Hp, 1668 c¡­N ®lLXÑ q­u­R 1668 c¡N pwœ²¡¿¹ Bl, Hp, eLp¡ h¡c£fr c¡¢Mm L­l­R Eš² eLp¡ cª­ø Hhw ¢X, X¢hÔE-1 Hl p¡rÉ fkÑ¡­m¡Qe¡ pÇf­LÑ fËa£uj¡e qu ®k, Eš² S¢j cMm J ec£­a i¡­‰ e¡Cz<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>kŸl©f Eš² i¨¢j Bl, Hp, S¢l­f 1 ew M¡p M¢au¡­e ®lLXÑ ¢m¢f ïj¡aÈL ¢p, Hp, 1003 c¡­Nl S¢j Bl Hp 1680-1684 ew c¡­N ®lLX Ñ q­u­R<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Eš² eLp¡ cª­ÖY~J Eš² c¡­Nl S¢j ec£ ¢p¢L¢Øa S¢j j­jÑ fËa£uj¡e<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>qu e¡ Hja¡hØq¡u e¡¢mn£ ‘M’ af¢p­ml S¢j Bl ,Hp, S¢l­f<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>plL¡­ll e¡­j 1M¡p<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>M¢au¡­e ®lLXÑ ¢m¢f<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>ïj¡aÚÈL ¢hd¡u<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>h¡c£ Bf£mL¡l£ fË¡¢bÑa j­a fË¢aL¡l<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>®f­a f¡­lz” </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above discussions and after perusal of the judgment and decree passed by the courts below I have carefully examined the findings of the courts below. I consider that the learned trial court committed no error of law by dismissing the suit on the ground that the plaintiff-opposite parties could not prove their case<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>with sufficient documents as to the title and possession which was<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>required under law from them, however the learned appellate court<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>below came to a wrongful conclusion to allow the appeal on the ground that the land was never diluviated despite the document produced by the parties, therefore, I consider that the learned appellate<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>court committed an error of law by allowing the appeal and by passing the impugned judgment and decree. I am therefore inclined to interfere into the judgment and decree passed by the appellate court below.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">        </span> </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Accordingly, I find merit in the Rule. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the result, the Rule is made absolute.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The Section is directed to communicate this judgment and decree to the concern Court below and also directed to send down the lower court records immediately. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--></span><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><span style="color: #000000;"> <!--[endif]--> </span><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__August__2019(2)/Issue%20__August__19(2)__C.%20Rule%203849%20of%2010_Md.%20Moinul%20Islam%20Chowdhury,%20J.__4.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">Civil </span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">Revision No. 3849 of 2010</span></u></strong></span></p></div></div></div></div>
786	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">BSMMU and others Vs. Dr. Zahidul Haq, (Hasan Foez Siddique, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NO. 3832 OF 2017  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Muhammad Imman Ali, J Hasan Foez Siddique, J, Mirza Hussain Haider, J Abu Bakar Siddiquee, J,  </p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Tanjib-ul Alam, Advocate instructed by Mr. Zainul Abedin, Advocate-on- Record. ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ AD</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujib Medical University represented by its Vice Chancellor and others </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Dr. Zahidul Haq </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Words and Phrases </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">(CIVIL)</span></strong></span></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 177px;" width="421"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 182.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mirza Hussain Haider, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Abu Bakar Siddiquee, J, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Judgment on</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">05.11.2018</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 30.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__August__2019(2)/Issue__August_19__C.%20P.%203832%20of%2017__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique_J___AD___3_.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in 0in 10.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 164.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujib Medical University represented by its Vice Chancellor and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . Petitioner</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;">Ve<span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">rsus</span></span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%; color: #000000;">Dr. Zahidul Haq</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 105%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;">...Respondent<u></u></span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12pt 0.85pt 0.0001pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Words and Phrases </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Experience </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Experience means a state, extent, or duration of being engaged in a particular </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">study or work. A word implying skill, facility,</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> or practical wisdom gained by personal knowledge, feeling, and action, and also the course or process by which one attains </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">knowledge or wisdom. The Law Lexicon says</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> experience means knowledge or practical wisdom gained from what one has observed, encountered or undergone.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">        </span>. . .
