(18)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Words and Phrases </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Employment advertisement </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">When an employment advertisement stipulates</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> a particular qualification as the minimum qualification for the post and further stipulates that the qualification should be relaxed in case of special qualification/ higher qualification the only meaning of it conveys is that some additional weightage has to be given to the higher qualified candidates.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                          </span>. . . (21)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Service matter—In the absence of rule or regulation selection committee do not require to record seasons—<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The selection has been made by the assessment of relative merits of rival candidates determined in the course of the interview of the candidates. There is no rule or regulation brought to our notice requiring the selection committee to record reasons. In the absence of any such legal requirment the selection made without recording reasons can not be found fault with. Administrative authority is under no legal obligation to record reasons in support of its decision. Indeed, even the principles of natural justice do not require a selection committee to record reasons for the selection or non-selection of a person in the absence of statutory requirement. But ‘fairness’ or ‘fair procedure’ ought to be observed.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>. . . (22)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: normal; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Shinda Hasan Vs. State of Uttar Pradesh and other AIR 1990 SC 1381 ref.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">For the Petitioner:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> Mr. Tanjib-ul Alam, Advocate instructed by Mr. Zainul Abedin, Advocate-on- Record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">For the Respondent :</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> Mr. Probir Neogi, Senior Advocate with Mr. A.M. Aminuddin, Senior Advocate and Mr. Mehadi Hasan Chowdhury, Ms. Anita Gazi Rahman, Advocate </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; letter-spacing: -0.2pt;">instructed by Mr. Md. Taufique</span><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> Hossain, Advocate-on-Record.</span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.85pt 12pt 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-variant: small-caps;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">This petition for leave to appeal is directed against the judgment and order dated 30.08.2015 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.1132 of 2011 making the Rule absolute.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">The facts, in brief, are that while the writ petitioner had been serving as Associate Professor in the Sylhet M.A.G. Osmani Medical College an employment notification was published for appointment in the post of Professor by the Bangabandhu Sheikh Mujib Medical University (the BSMMU). In the said notification, the wanting experience, amongst others, was that the applicant must have five years experience in performing the functions as Associate Professor of that particular subject regularly or teaching experience in equal status. The writ petitioner, finding him qualified for the post, filed application stating his educational qualifications, length of experience and other particulars. Following the regular recruitment procedure, he was selected as a Professor of Surgery on 10.09.2003 by the BSMMU authority. Since the writ petitioner was in government service he filed application addressing the Secretary, Ministry of Health and Family Welfare on 22.09.2003 tendering his resignation with effect from 30.09.2003. Pursuant to his application, his resignation was accepted with effect from 30.09.2003. Getting appointment, he joined in the BSMMU on 01.10.2003. The writ petitioner had resigned from his government job without taking any financial benefit. The appointment of the writ petitioner was made in strict and full compliance of the provisions followed for appointment of a Professor of the BSMMU which was approved by the Syndicate of the BSMMU in its 16th meeting held on 03.03.2004. The service of the writ petitioner was confirmed by the Syndicate of the BSMMU on 13.08.2004 in its 21st meeting. The writ petitioner, at the time of filing application for recruitment, did not suppress anything with regard to his qualifications, experiences and publications etc. At the time of appointment of the writ petitioner, he had the highest number of post graduation degrees and he was the only person who had fellowship in colorectal surgery from the National University Hospital, Singapore. The writ petitioner earned reputation as one of the best doctors of the country. Due to his unblemished service record and ability, he was given the charge of Course Co-ordinator of all Post Graduate Courses and the Residency Programmes run by the Surgery Department of the BSMMU. During his entire service career, no question was raised with regard to his ability and competency as a doctor and a teacher. In the absence of the Chairman of the Surgery Department, he was given the charge of Chairmanship on many occasions. He was also a member of the Departmental Examination Committee. While the writ petitioner was discharging his duties with highest level of satisfaction of the BSMMU authority, all on a sudden, he was served with a notice vide an office order dated 30.06.2010 <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">under Memo No. BSMMU/2010/7060 to explain</span> as to why his appointment in the BSMMU would not be cancelled. The writ petitioner was asked to submit his reply, if any, within 7 days from the date of receipt of the order. Without considering the reply, the BSMMU authority vide the impugned order dated 22.12.2010 under Memo No. BSMMU/ 2010/12315 had terminated the writ petitioner from service in the name of ‘cancellation of appointment’ allegedly on the basis of the decision of the Syndicate dated 22.12.2010. Challenging the order of cancellation of appointment dated 22.12.2010 the writ petitioner, filing writ petition, obtained Rule Nisi.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">The writ respondent Nos.1-3 contested the Rule contending that on 25.06.2003, the BSMMU authority published an advertisement for appointment of suitable candidates for the several vacant posts under the BSMMU. On 10.09.2003, the writ petitioner was selected for the post of Professor of Surgery Department by the then administration of the BSMMU. Subsequently, it was revealed that the writ petitioner had no necessary experience and qualifications for such appointment and his appointment to the post of Professor was secured not through meeting the relevant recruitment criteria but through some other means which does not necessarily make his appointment legal and hence his appointment was a nullity. During the past Care-taker Government, allegation of corruption, irregularities in purchase and recruitments were brought against the then administration of the BSMMU which were referred to the then Vice Chancellor of the University by the office of the Head of the care-taker government through the concerned Ministry. The BSMMU authority constituted a 7(seven) members Enquiry Committee vide Memo dated 06.05.2007. The Enquiry Committee, holding inquiry, submitted report on 26.07.2007 stating that the writ petitioner failed to meet the required experience to be appointed as professor and hence proper steps as per law should be taken against the appointment process of the writ petitioner. Thereafter, another 6(six) members <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Committee was formed by the then administration</span> of the BSMMU dated 05.08.2007. The Committee found that the writ petitioner did <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">not meet the experience required to be appointed</span> in the post of professor. Subsequently, the Parliamentary Standing Committee of the Ministry of Health and Family Welfare decided to hold enquire into the allegations of corruption and irregularities committed in the BSMMU and submit detailed report before the Parliamentary Standing Committee. A Sub Committee, holding inquiry, submitted a detailed report before the Standing Committee on 12.01.2010 stating, inter alia, that in the appointment process the relevant rules and regulations had not been followed. The writ petitioner was appointed despite his lacking of required experience for appointment. In that <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">report, it was recommended that the appointment</span> of writ petitioner should be cancelled since he did not hold necessary experience at the time of appointment as Professor of Surgery. On 16.05.2010 in the 38th Syndicate Meeting of the BSMMU, the authority decided to take necessary steps and to that end, writ petitioner was served with a show cause notice through the Office Order bearing Memo No. BSMMU /2010/7060 dated 30.06.2010 asking him to furnish reasons within 7(seven) days as to why his appointment in the post of Professor of Surgery should not be cancelled in view of the report of the Committee. The writ petitioner upon receiving the said show cause notice submitted his reply on 04.07.2010 and on perusal of the same the Syndicate, in its 41st meeting held on 22.12.2010, decided to cancel the appointment of the writ petitioner in the post of Professor by the impugned letter dated 22.12.2010. On 16.01.2011, upon receipt of the said cancellation letter from the university, the writ petitioner filed a Review petition to the office of Chancellor of the BSMMU through writ respondent No.3 instead of the Vice Chancellor as required under section 55 of the Act, 1998. Thereafter, the writ petitioner filed the instant writ petition and obtained Rule which was liable to be discharged.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The High Court Division by the impugned judgment and order made the said Rule absolute. Against which, the BSMMU has filed this petition for leave to appeal.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Tanjib-ul Alam, learned Counsel appearing for the writ respondent-petitioner, submits that at the time of appointing the writ petitioner he had no requisite experience to be appointed in the post of Professor of the University and the then BSMMU authority most illegally appointed him as Professor of the surgery department, thus, the BSMMU authority rightly cancelled his appointment, the High Court Division erred in law in making the Rule absolute.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Probir Neogi, appearing with Mr. A.M. Aminuddin, Mr. Mehadi Hasan Chowdhury, Ms. Anita Gazi, learned Counsel for the respondent, submits that the writ petitioner-respondent had requisite qualifications and experiences to be appointed as professor of the department of the BSMMU and the BSMMU auhority, being satisfied with the same and complying with all legal formalities, appointed the writ petitioner in the said post. Moreso, in the advertisement, it was mentioned that the terms and conditions as mentioned in employment notification would be relaxed for the candidate having special qualifications, the High Court Division rightly made the Rule absolute. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">From the papers available in the record, it appears that the BSMMU authority issued employment notification under memo No. </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">we Gm <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Gg Gg BD/2003/35/32</span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.2pt;"> dated 24.06.2003 inviting</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> application for appointment in the post of Professors and in some other posts. In the said notification it was specifically mentioned, </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Courier;">“</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">we‡kl †hvM¨Zvm¤úboe cªv_©x‡`i †¶‡Î †h †Kvb kZ© wkw_j‡hvM¨|</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Courier;">”</span> <span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">For getting appointment in the post of professor of the BSMMU the required qualifications, experiences and other particulars as provided in the notification were as follows:</span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: BurigangaSushreeMJ;">Òe½eÜz †kL gywRe †gwWK¨vj wek¡we`¨vjq</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 22.5pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 8pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: BurigangaSushreeMJ;">mycvwikt</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 8pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: BurigangaSushreeMJ;">(K) wb‡qvMKvjxb mg‡q AwfÁZvi kZ© c~iY bv nIqvi wb‡qvM cªvß e¨w³i Aa¨vcK c‡` wb‡qvM wewam¤§Z nq bvB weavq Zuvi wb‡qvM evwZj Kivi mycvwik Kiv nj|</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 8pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: BurigangaSushreeMJ;">(L) wek¡we`¨vj‡qi wb‡qvM wewa Abyhvqx wbw`©ó c‡` wb‡qv‡Mi kZ©vejx c~iY bv nIqv m‡Ë¡I GB cªv_©x‡K wbe©vPb K‡i‡Qb| G‡Z wb‡qvM KwgwUi ZrKvjxb mfvcwZ, m`m¨MY I m`m¨-mwPe wbqg msNb I KZ©e¨ Ae‡njv K‡i‡Qb e‡j cªZxqgvb nq weavq Zuv‡`i weiy‡× AvBbvbyM e¨e¯nv Mªn‡Yi mycvwik Kiv nj|</span></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12pt 0in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Precisely, the allegation against the writ petitioner, as it appears from subsequent inquiry reports that at the time of getting appointment as professor in the BSMMU he had no requisite experience. More specifically, in the employment notification required experience for filing application in the post of professor was that, </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Courier;">“</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">wbw`©ó wel‡q wbqwgZ cuvP erm‡ii mn‡hvMx Aa¨vcK A_ev mgvb c` gh©v`vi wk¶KZv</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Courier;">”</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> but the writ petitioner had no such experience. He had following teaching experience at the relevant time:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 3pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">(1)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>Associate Professor (Current charge)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 3pt 45pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Moymonshingh Medical College </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 45.35pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">(from 01.03.1998 to 31.05.1998)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 3pt 27.35pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">(2)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>Associate Professor (current charge)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 3pt 45.35pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">BSMMU</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 45.35pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">(from 01.06.1998 to 09.05.2001)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 3pt 27.35pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">(3)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>Associate Professor</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 3pt 45pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Sylhet M.A.G. Osmani Medical College</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 45pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">(from 09.05.2001 to 30.09.2003)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">That is, he had 5 years 04 months 15 days teaching experience as Associate Professor in charge and Associate Professor before filing application. It appears that the writ petitioner, holding the post of Associate Professor, performed his duties more than 2 years and holding the post of Associate Professor-in-charge performed his duties for more than 3 years. Question is, whether at the time of performing his duties as Associate Professor in charge he had acquired any experience or not. According to Black’s Law Dictionary experience means a state, extent, or duration of being engaged in a particular study or work. A word implying skill, facility, or practical wisdom gained by personal knowledge, feeling, and action, and also the course or process by which one attains knowledge or wisdom. The Law Lexicon says experience means knowledge or practical wisdom gained from what one has observed, encountered or undergone. While performing the functions of a Associate professor-in-charge the same was not the substantive post of the writ petitioner but it is difficult to say conclusively that within those period he did not gather any experience as Associate Professor-in-Charge or his skill has not been improved. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have already found from the advertisement that it was mentioned specially therein that every condition is relaxable in the case of special qualifications of the candidate. The exact words were, </span><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Courier;">“</span></u><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">we‡kl †hvM¨Zvm¤úbœ cªv_©x‡`i †¶‡Î †h †Kvb kZ© wkw_j‡hvM¨</span></u></strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Courier;">”</span></u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">.(underlined by us) </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.2pt;">From the required education qualifications</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> for the post of Professor in respect of clinical subject as mentioned in the employment notification issued by the BSMMU authority as well as in </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Courier;">“</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">wb‡qvM bxwZgvjv (wk¶K)</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyMJ;">t</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Courier;">”</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> were No.(1)MBBS or equal degree, (2) MD in particular subject or MS (from the BSMMU or Dhaka University)/ FCPS (Fellowship of the College of Physicians and Surgeons of Bangladesh) /MRCP, FRCS, MRCOG DMRT /DRMD/ DPM/ M/M. Phil or post graduate or any post graduate qualification in equal status. That is, the writ petitioner was entitled to file application for getting appointment in BSMMU since, at the relevant time, he had MBBS and FCPS degrees. It further appears that apart from MBBS and FCPS degrees, the writ petitioner had FRCS degree from the Royal College of Physicians and Surgeons of Glasgow, UK, MS(Surgery) from the Institute of Postgraduate Medicine and Research, Dhaka (Dhaka University), Bangladesh and Fellowship of Colorectal Surgery from the National University Hospital, Singapore. That is, he acquired specific surgical qualification, that was, Fellowship of the Royal College of Surgeons which is training in surgical specialities and which also shows his education and training, professional qualifications, and surgical competence which was given upon rigorous evaluation and which is consistent with high standards of special qualification. It further appears that in addition to his FCPS and FRCS decrees, he had also M.S. (Surgery) degree which is also a postgraduate degree and advanced qualification in surgery. The said degree is also designed to be awarded as a higher degree. That is, the writ petitioner had special qualifications to be appointed as Professor of the BSMMU. It is quite clear that the petitioner had post graduation degrees and Fellowships for meeting the eligibility criteria, for filing applications in the post of Professor. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have already found that in the advertisement it was specifically mentioned that in case of special qualifications every terms and conditions mentioned in the employment notification was relaxable. When an employment advertisement stipulates a particular qualification as the minimum qualification for the post and further stipulates that the qualification should be relaxed in case of special qualification/higher qualification the only meaning of it conveys is that some additional weightage has to be given to the higher qualified candidates. The writ petitioner had three more special qualifications, that is, FRCS, MS (Surgery) and Fellowship of colorectal surgery, National University Hospital, Singapore besides the requisite qualification as mentioned in the employment notification. From the first inquiry report held by the BSMMU it appears that the BSMMU syndicate in its 21st meeting decided that in case of specially qualified candidates the terms as provided is relaxable and in the said report it was further observed that, </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: BurigangaSushreeMJ;">“<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">eZ©gvb ch©v‡jvPbv KwgwU wek¡we`¨vj‡qi Rb¥j‡Mœ 30/04/1998Bs Zvwi‡L RvixK…Z ZrKvjxb wfwm AavcK Gg, G Kv‡`ix g‡nv`‡qi ¯^v¶‡i GKwU Awdm Av‡`‡k †`Lv‡Z cvq †h, mv‡eK AvBwcwRGgGÛAvi Gi 43 Rb wk¶K‡K Zuv‡`i K…Z c~e© PvKzixi PjwZ `vwqZ¡ Ges fvicªvß c‡`i AwfÁZv‡K we‡ePbv K‡i ¯e-¯e c‡` GB wek¡we`¨vj‡qi PvKzix‡Z wbqwgZ Kiv n‡q‡Q|</strong>”</span> <span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In such view of the matter, it is difficult to hold that writ petitioner’s appointment was totally illegal. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have found that in another Inquiry report it has been observed, </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: BurigangaSushreeMJ;">“<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">ÒcwÎKvq cªKvwkZ wb‡qvM weÁwß‡Z D‡jøwLZ Ôwe‡kl †hvM¨Zv m¤úbœ cªv_©x‡`i †¶‡Î †h †Kvb kZ© wkw_j †hvM¨Õ Gi mg_©‡b cªv_©xi wK we‡kl †hvM¨Zv wQj Ges †Kvb we‡kl †hvM¨Zvi wfwË‡Z wb‡qvM kZ© wkw_j Kiv n‡qwQj wKbv, †m m¤ú‡K© wb‡qvM KwgwUi Kvh©weeibx‡Z †Kvb wKQy D‡jøL bvB|</strong>Ó</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Courier;">”</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> The selection has been made by the assessment of relative merits of rival candidates determined in the course of the interview of the candidates. There is no rule or regulation brought to our notice requiring the selection committee to record reasons. In the absence of any such legal requirment the selection made without recording reasons can not be found fault with. Administrative authority is under no legal obligation to record reasons in support of its decision. Indeed, even the principles of natural justice do not require a selection committee to record reasons for the selection or non-selection of a person in the absence of statutory requirement. But ‘fairness’ or ‘fair procedure’ ought to be observed. It is not shown that the selection was arbitrary or whimsical or the selection committee did not act fairly in appointing Dr. Zahidul Huq. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It is relevant here to refer the case of Ms. Shinda Hasan V. State of Uttar Pradesh and other reported in AIR 1990 SC 1381. In the said case in response to the advertisement the appellant along with others applied for the post. The appellant did not fulfill the qualification of five years experience. She alone appeared for the interview and the Selection Committee relaxed the qualification of experience in her favour and selected her. The Management thereafter sought the approval of the University to appoint the appellant as required under section 31(11) of the Uttar Pradesh State Universities Act, 1973. The University, however, declined to approve and directed the management to re-advertise the post. The appellant challenged the decision of the University by way of a writ petition under Article 226 of the Constitution of India before the Luckhnow Bench of the Allahabad High Court on the ground that the college being a minority institution any interference by the University under the Act is violative of Article 30(1) of the Constitution. It was also contended that there was no basis of justification to withhold the approval. The High Court rejected the attack on the ground of Article 30 of the Constitution of India by holding that the provisions of the Act are regulatory and are primarily for the purpose of maintaining uniformity, efficiency and standards of education in the minority institutions. On the merits, the High Court held that the Selection Committee was not justified in relaxing the qualification without reserving that right to itself in the advertisement. The High Court also found that the qualification ‘possessing working knowledge of Urdu’ was unjust. On the above findings the writ petition was dismissed. This is how the appellant went to the Supreme Court. Supreme Court adjourned the case with the following order: ‘It is admitted by the parties that as a result of the Court orders the appellant Ms. Shainda Hasan is continuing to work as Principal in the Karamat Husain Muslim Girls College, Lucknow since 1974. Having served the institution for over 16 years it would be unjust to make her leave the post. Under the circumstances let the University reconsider the whole matter sympathetically.’” Then Indian Supreme Court of India held, </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 30pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">“Keeping in view the facts and circumstances of the case and in the interest of justice we direct the Luckhnow University and its Vice-Chancellor to grant the necessary approval to the appointment of the appellant as Principal of Karamat Husain Muslim Girls College, Luckhnow, with effect from the date she is holding the said post. We further direct that the appellant shall be entitled to the salary, allowances and all other consequential benefits to which a regular principal of the said college would have been and is entitled.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">This case is better than that of the above referred case since there was a clause in employment notification of relaxation of every terms of qualifications in case of special qualifications which the writ petitioner had. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">From the employment notification, appointment of the writ petitioner, service of the petitioner as professor for about 7 years in the BSMMU and that after cancellation of his appointment, the repeated request of the BSMMU authority to take class in FCPS and MS (final) course in the BSMMU and from repeated inquiries and reports of the Inquiry Committees it appears to us that the turnabout of the BSMMU authority in flip-flop flipin stance has put the writ petitioner in a predicament which should be deprecated.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We are of the view that conclusion arrived at by the High Court Division does not calls for any interference.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Accordingly, the petition is dismissed.</span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-left: 27.35pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Ed.</strong> </span></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--></span><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><span style="color: #000000;"> <!--[endif]--> </span><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__August__2019(2)/Issue__August_19__C.%20P.%203832%20of%2017__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique_J___AD___3_.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Civil petition for leave to appeal No. 3832 of 2017.</span></u></em></strong></a><u></u></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">(From the judgment and order dated 30.08.2015 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No. 1132 of 2011.)</span></span></p></div></div></div></div>
787	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Hazera Khatun &amp; others Vs. Dr. Md. Ismail Hossain &amp; others, (Soumendra Sarker, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Rule No. 15(con) of 2018  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Soumendra Sarker, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Abdul Haque, Advocate ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Hazera Khatun and others  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Dr. Md. Ismail Hossain and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Limitation Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; font-variant: small-caps;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 232px;" width="468"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 204.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Soumendra Sarker, J</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">17.01.2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 35.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__August__2019(2)/Issue%20__August__19(2)__C.%20Rule%2015%20con%20of%2018_Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J.__1.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 184.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Hazera Khatun and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Defendant-Respondent -Petitioners</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Dr. Md. Ismail Hossain and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Plaintiff-Appellant- Opposite parties.</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: left;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Limitation Act (IX o</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">f 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 5</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Delay due to wrong but bona fide advice may be a good ground for condoning the delay but it ought to have given on bona fide impression. The mistaken advice given by a legal practitioner may in the circumstances of a particular case, give rise to sufficient cause within the meaning of this section 5 of the Limitation Act, provided the advice should be bona fide and without any malice. There is nothing on record to hold such a view that wrong information which was given to the applicants by their engaged Lawyer was not bona fide rather mala fide. It is also no where within the connected </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">papers that the defendant-petitioner-applicants</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> were negligent or that they had any willful laches in preferring the revisional application within time. Hence, the delay of 2037 in filing the civil revision which is inordinate was caused not for the laches or negligence of the petitioner-applicants, but it was due to unavoidable circumstances as alleged from the side of the petitioner-applicants in their application for condonation of delay. The law of limitation enjoys that the delay in filing the revisional application, whatever it may, can be condoned if the applicant can satisfy the court that he had sufficient cause. In the instant case, the petitioner-applicants have been able to justify their case that there were not negligent or inactive in bringing their case within time.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">     </span>. . . .(8 and 11)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Md. Abdul Haque, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the petitioners</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">No one appears </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the opposite parties</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Soumendra Sarker</span></u></strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">, J. </span></u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The Rule issued calling upon the opposite parties No. 1-13 to show cause as to why the delay of 2037 days in filing the revisional application should not be condoned and/or pass such other order or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The facts leading to the issuance of the Rule in a nutshell can be stated thus, the present opposite parties as plaintiffs instituted the original Suit for Partition being No. 229 of 1991 in the Additional Court of the learned Assistant Judge, Sadar, Mymensingh against the present Defendant-Respondent- Petitioners and the suit was decreed in the preliminary form on 30.11.1997.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved the present opposite parties filed an appeal being Title Appeal No. 44 of 1998 in the court of the learned District Judge, Mymensingh which was transmitted to the 2<sup>nd</sup> court of the learned Additional District Judge, Mymensingh for hearing and disposal. The learned Appellate Court on hearing the appeal allowed the appeal and passed a revised preliminary decree on 05.03.2012.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned judgment and decree the Defendant-Petitioners have preferred a civil revision under section 115 (1) of the Code of Civil Procedure before this court, but in filing the civil revision there has been a delay of 2037 days. For condonation of the said delay, the Defendant-Respondent-Petitioners have filed an application under section 05 of the Limitation Act, 1908 and obtained this Rule. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">During hearing of this Rule Mr. Md. Abdul Haque the learned Advocate appeared on behalf of the petitioners, while none appears on behalf of the opposite parties.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%;">The learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioners submits that the petitioners were all along vigilant and diligent in filing the civil revision, but for the reason stated in their application for condonation of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span><span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">delay, the delay occurred, which is unintentional</span> and not for the laches or negligence of the Defendant-Respondent-Petitioners. The learned Advocate further submits that after pronouncement of the impugned judgment and decree dated 05.03.2012, the learned Advocate who was engaged on behalf of the petitioners in the Appellate Court wrongly informed the Defendant No. 20(Ka)- 20(Jha) that their application for saham has been allowed by the Appellate Court and for the said reason the Defendant-Petitioners did not feel any necessity to proceed against the judgment and decree of the Appellate Court dated 05.03.2012. The learned Advocate also submits that in the month of October, 2017 the present petitioners came to know that some of the defendants of the Partition Suit No. 229 of 1991 preferred Civil Revision No. 1207 of 2012 and 1208 of 2012 and Rule has been issued in both the civil revisions and the operation of the impugned judgment and decree dated 05.03.2017 has been stayed. The petitioners in those civil revisions not impleaded the present petitioners in their revisional applications. Thereafter the petitioners knowing about those civil revisions filed an application for addition of party in Civil Revision No. 1207 of 2012 and pursuant to that, they have been added as opposite parties No. 85-91 in that Civil Revision No. 1207 of 2012. At this stage, the learned Advocate for the petitioners going through the judgment of the Appellate Court on 28.12.2017 disclosed before the petitioners that the petitioners have been allowed a separate saham for .01625 acres of land, although the petitioners prayed for getting a separate saham to the extent of .0462 acres of land. Knowing about that, the petitioners felt aggrieved and decided to prefer a civil revision against the judgment and decree of the Appellate Court and accordingly, requested their engaged Advocate to file civil revision against the judgment and decree dated 05.03.2012. The learned Advocate lastly submits that, receiving the papers for filing of the civil revision, after drafting the revisional<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>application he has filed the revisional application, but meanwhile a delay of 2037 days occurred, which is unintentional<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and not for the negligence of the petitioner-applicants. The learned Advocate also submits that the petitioners were wrongly informed initially by their engaged Lawyer of the appellate court that they have obtained their prayed saham and due to that wrong<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>information of the then Advocate of the petitioners, the petitioners could not bring the revisional application within time and thereby the cause of delay is <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> and purely for the wrong information and misrepresentation of the learned Advocate for the petitioners, who was engaged in conducting<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the appeal before the appellate court and as such the learned Advocate prays for condonation of the delay. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In order to appreciate the submission advanced from the side of the learned Counsel for the petitioners, having gone through the judgment and decree passed by the trial court dated 30.11.1997 in the original Partition Suit No. 229 of 1991 along with the impugned judgment and decree passed by the Appellate Court on 05.03.2012 in other Appeal No. 44 of 1998 and the relevant papers, it transpires that, it was the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>specific case of the present petitioner-applicants in their application for getting a separate saham that they are entitled a separate saham for a land measuring .0462 acres and in this context, obviously it is noticed from the impugned judgment and decree that the petitioner-applicants were allowed a separate saham for .01625 acres of land in the suit holding and these applicants were the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>defendants No. 20(Ka)-20 (Jha) to the original suit. It is also the specific contention of the Petitioner-Applicants that inasmuch as, their the then engaged Lawyer wrongly informed them that the appellate court by its judgment and decree dated 05.03.2012 allowed a separate saham in favour of the present Defendant-Respondent-Petitioners according to their prayer and for that reason, the Defendants No. 20(Kha)-20(Jha) that their application for saham have been allowed by the Appellate Court, the Defendant-Respondent-Petitioners did not feel any necessity to proceed against the judgment and decree dated 05.03.2012. It was further contended from the side of the applicants in their application for condonation of delay that for the 1<sup>st</sup> time on 28.12.2017 they came to know from their engaged Lawyer that they have been allowed a less quantum of land than that of their prayed quantum of land and instead of .0462 acres of land, they were given .01625 acres of land and at that time the petitioners felt aggrieved and being dissatisfied with the judgment and decree passed by the Appellate Court, they have decided to prefer Civil Revision. It is the specific case of the petitioner-applicants that for the wrong information and misrepresentation of their earlier engaged Advocate of the Appellate Court, the petitioners could not prefer the civil revision within time and the petitioners as such were prevented by sufficient cause in not bringing the civil revision within the statutory<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>period of limitation. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 05 of the law of limitation (Act IX of 1908) contemplates that, delay due to wrong but <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> advice of the Lawyer can be treated sufficient explanation of delay. The Lawyer’s wrong advice may be a good ground for condoning the delay but it ought to have given on <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide </em>impression. The mistaken advice given by a legal practitioner may in the circumstances of a particular case, give rise to sufficient cause within the meaning of this section 05 of the Limitation Act, provided the advice should be <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and without any malice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the instant case, I have come across from the facts and circumstances of the case that the present applicants who are the defendants No. 20 (Kha)-20(Jha) in their application for getting a separate saham in the original partition suit prayed for .0462<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>acres of land in the suit holding. But in the ordering portion of the impugned judgment and decree dated 05.03.2012, the learned Additional District Judge, 2<sup>nd</sup> Court, Mymensingh allowed them only .01625 acres of land instead of .0462 acres, and in this regard it is the specific case of the present petitioners that their the then engaged Lawyer upon whom the defendant-respondent-applicants were fully dependent, inasmuch as, they are not the law knowing persons and villagers, misinformed them that they have been allowed their prayed saham and for the said reason the petitioner-applicants did not feel any necessity to proceed against the judgment and decree dated 05.03.2012. It is likely for the petitioner-appellants who are not the law<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>knowing persons or well conversant about the proceedings of a case, were fully dependent<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>upon their engaged lawyer who informed them wrongly about the judgment and decree passed by the Appellate Court after pronouncement of the judgment on 05.03.2012.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The original Other Class Suit No. 229 of 1991 was a suit for partition, which was among the co-sharers of the suit holding and admittedly the petitioner-applicants were the co-sharers and they submitted their pleading’s case<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>in the form of written statement before the learned trial court.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The specific contention which is given from the side of the defendant-petitioner-applicants is not challenged from any corner and the plaintiffs to the original suit who are the present opposite parties did not controvert the submission advanced from the side of the petitioner-applicants, rather; they remained silent, which is a strong circumstantial<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>evidence in support of the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> of the petitioner-applicants. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">There is nothing on record to hold such a view that the wrong information which was given to the applicants by their engaged Lawyer was not <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> rather <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">mala fide</em>. It is also no where within the connected papers that <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the defendant-petitioner-applicants were negligent</span> or that they had any willful laches in preferring the revisional application within time. Hence, I find that the delay which is inordinate<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>was caused not for the laches or negligence of the <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">petitioner-applicants, but it was due to unavoidable</span> circumstances as alleged from the <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">side of the Petitioner-applicants in their application</span> for <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">condonation of delay. The law of limitation enjoys</span> <span style="letter-spacing: -.1pt;">that the delay in filing the revisional application,</span> </span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">what ever it may,  can be condoned if the applicant can satisfy the court that he had sufficient cause. In the instant case, the Petitioner-applicants have been able to justify their case that there were not negligent or inactive in bringing their case within time. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">12.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Be that as it may, I am constrained to hold such a view that the cause of delay is <em>bona fide</em> and not for the laches or negligence of the petitioner-applicants, rather; the petitioners were due diligent in getting their relief as prayed for.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">13.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Having regard to the facts, circumstances and the discussions referred to above, I am constrained to hold such a view that he rule has got substance to succeed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">14.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the result; the Rule is made absolute without any order as to costs. The delay of 2037 days in filing the revisional application is hereby condoned. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">15.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Office is directed to do the needful at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 24.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 24.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__August__2019(2)/Issue%20__August__19(2)__C.%20Rule%2015%20con%20of%2018_Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J.__1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">Civil </span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Vrinda;">Rule No. 15(con) of 2018</span></u></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
788	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Kay and Que (BD) Ltd. Vs.  Registrar, Joint Stock Co., (Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Cmpany Matter No. 256 of 2018  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Rafique-ul Huq, Senior Advocate with Mr. Margub Kabir, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Kay and Que (Bangladesh) Limited </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  The Registrar, Joint Stock Companies and Firms, Dhaka and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Company Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(STATUTORY ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 201px;" width="519"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 228.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">11.03.2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 39.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue__August__2019(2)/Issue%20__August__19(2)__Company__256%20of%2018_Muhammad%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarkar,%20J.__7.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 207.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Kay and Que (Bangladesh) Limited</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Transferee-petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">MultiSourcing Limited </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Transferor-petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The Registrar, Joint Stock Companies and Firms, Dhaka and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Respondents </span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Company Act (XVIII of 1994)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 228</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Any company incorporated under the Companies Act may embody in its object clause the provisions for amalgamation with any other company or body of persons and, in the event that the draftsman of the MoA omits to inscribe the provision, it can be inserted therein with the approval of the Court. If the provision for amalgamation is not contained in the MoA of the company, it cannot take a decision for amalgamation in </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">that, MoA of any incorporated company having</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> the status of law, any act not authorised by the MoA is ultra vires the law.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                          </span>. . . (33)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Company Act (XVIII of 1994)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 228(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Legal procedures for amalgamation of the companies:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">When two or more companies become desirous to enter into any arrangement of merger with each other towards converting themselves into one single entity, they all, as the petitioners, would make an application to the Court under sub-Section (1) of Section 228 of the Companies Act for directions for convening of the meetings of the members and creditors, if any, for considering the proposed Scheme of Amalgamation, at first. On such an application, the Court would issue directions for convening of separate meetings of the members and/or creditors or different classes of members and/or creditors, as the case may be. In the said meetings of the members and/or creditors, the Scheme of Amalgamation is required to be approved by majority in number representing three-fourths in value of the creditors or class of creditors or members or class of members, as the case may be. After the Scheme is approved by all concerned in their respective meetings, a separate petition then would be presented to the Court for sanctioning of the Scheme of Amalgamation. However, if the prayer for sanctioning of the Scheme of Amalgamation has already been made in the original application, there is no need to file a separate application, but in that event, the fact as to the approval by the three-fourths in value of the members/ creditors should be brought to the notice of this Court by way of filing a supplementary affidavit.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>. . . (40)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Company Act (XVIII of 1994)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 228(2)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Why the presence of the three-fourths of the shareholders is required:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The decision approving the Scheme of Amalgamation should be passed by majority in number representing three-fourths in value of the members or class of members and/or creditors or class of creditors, as the case may be, in order to make the said decision binding upon all the shareholders, creditors and the company.
